## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / biological population growth
**Analysis**: This is a single-species population dynamics task where the growth rate dP_dt depends on time t and current population P. It belongs to population ecology, focusing on models of how populations change over time, possibly including density-dependent regulation, time-varying environments, or alternative growth paradigms beyond simple logistic growth.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted Malthusian growth)
- Logistic differential: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (symmetric density-dependent regulation, carrying capacity 1/c1)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric S-shaped growth, heavier tail towards carrying capacity)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**(c1) - c2 * P (allometric growth with anabolic and catabolic terms, often c1=2/3)
- Richards growth differential: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density-dependent shape with asymmetry parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (growth intermediate only above threshold c1 and below carrying capacity c2)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) + c3 * P (possible positive growth even below threshold)
- Logistic with time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (linearly changing environment)
- Seasonal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (sinusoidal environmental variation)
- Time lag logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 * exp(-c2 * t) (decaying density dependence mimicking delayed response)
- Power-law growth with saturation: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (two-term balance)
- Time-dependent intrinsic growth: dP_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * P (declining growth rate over time)
- Generalised logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - (c2 * P)**c3) (rich form for complex scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- S-shaped population curve (slow start, rapid growth, saturation) → dP_dt is hump-shaped function of P, e.g., P*(1-P/K)
- Density-dependent negative feedback → term like -c*P^2 or -c*P^a with a>1 to reduce growth at high P
- Allee effects (low population density reduces growth) → dP_dt negative or reduced when P is small, e.g., (P-A) factor
- Time-varying carrying capacity → K appears as function of t, e.g., linear, exponential, or periodic
- Allometric scaling (metabolism/growth) → P raised to a fractional power like 2/3 or 3/4
- Asymptotic mass/size (von Bertalanffy) → growth rate as difference between anabolic term ~P^(c) and catabolic term ~P
- Time-dependent intrinsic growth rate → explicit multiplication by decreasing exp(-t) or 1/(1+t) to model aging environment
- Seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing → additive sine/cosine terms on dP_dt
- Gompertz-type asymmetry → growth deceleration depends on log(P), heavier when near carrying capacity
- Richards curve asymmetry → extra exponent on normalized density (P/K)^c allows inflected sigmoid with adjustable asymmetry
